Its no exception that \\"Sunken Condos\\" provides that same sound and is proudly welcomed into the Fagen archives of good music.<br />  The Nightfly Trilogy was scattered in years but overly successful in keeping the music relatively close, giving no hint of adaptation to current music fads or styles.  Fagen always stuck to the basics, satisfying all fans alike regardless of the time period.  \\"Sunken Condos\\" is equally achieving as each song is produced with strong elements from Fagen and Leonhart alike.<br /><br />  \\"Slinky Thing\\" opens the album with an armed funk session that would have even Gary Katz moving his hips. Good bass lines here and the guitar solo by Jon Herington provides a \\"Two Against Nature\\" vibe.<br /><br />  \\"I'm Not The Same Without You\\" speeds it up a little with good lyrics and a touch of \\"Nightfly\\" with the harmonica session.  \\"Without you, I now have eyes to see.  Some other destiny, a futurescape of bright arcades.  Definitely Fagen back at it! This song could clearly but missing from the Gaucho sessions.<br /><br />  \\"Memorablilia\\" is has a strong sound that could insert itself to the \\"Everything Must Go\\" album and the chorus here is a plus.  The horns are very appropriate on this track and are hardly noticeable but makes a statement when the horn solo arrives.<br /><br />  \\"The New Breed\\" is a wow of a song, good crooning guitar riffs, soul vibes and echoing backing vocals.  Amazing how Fagen's voice is still keeping it's touch!<br /><br />  \\"Miss Marlene\\" would probably be a highlight for me as the track is kept smooth, jazzy, and tips the hat to the Kamakiriad days.<br /><br />  Donald Fagen proves that he hasn't lost his touch and isn't afraid to step away from the Nightfly Trilogy tone as this one is a little more soulfoul than the previous ones.  Even though it's different from the previous days, it's definitely a strong album to fit with Steely Dan albums.  All tracks are evident with a wide range of instruments once again provided with backing vocals to give it the Fagen feel.  Do not count the album short.  The sound is respectfully close to Gaucho and Babylon Sisters would clearly make this sound its sibling in many ways.  A must purchase and would test any surround system any day.

0452289963|5.0|I looked at this book last year when Oprah had her series with him, and for whatever reason it did not resonate. I had read his book The Power of Now years ago and found it esoteric and 'heavy going' (too 'heady' and abstract for me at the time.)<br /><br />But I happened to be at Bart's Books in Ojai this weekend and picked this up. My friend and I were there on a kind of inspirational/contemplative getaway and the book seemed fitting fare to imbibe on the four hour train ride home.<br /><br />The phrase when the student is ready the teacher appears is what comes to mind. His message, most particularly the section about the 'pain body' and the ego and their cooperation with each other, just hit me like a thunderclap.<br /><br />Now I had spent the weekend being 'triggered' by someone I found obtuse, oblivious, thoughtless and even deceptive (our hostess at the BnB type place we stayed at). I spent a chunk of time fuming over how I wasn't getting what I paid for etc. Then in talking to my friend I realized I had had this SAME experience at least three other occasions in the past! Stayed somewhere where the female hostess/proprietor was unwell, unavailable, and not offering the level of service their reviews and marketing claimed they had.<br /><br />And when I read on the train about pain bodies, how we are all born with them, they vary in strength and activity, but when they are recognized (observed with neutrality), when events and the ego conspire to 'feed them' with stories of 'they did it again! this always happens to me! I recognized what had happened to me and in an instant the indignation melted into bemusement and I did indeed observe that the blocked energy of the pain body transmuted into a beautiful kind of awareness.<br /><br />In describing my epiphany to someone today I likened the pain body to the Wicked Witch of the West in Wizard of Oz who dissolves when pure water (awareness/ presence) is thrown on her.<br /><br />Our ego is clever and fancy and often the more 'intellectual' our tendencies, the more 'enlightened' and special we deem ourselves, the more 'defended' and blind we can be.<br /><br />The triggering event that provokes our outrage contains a beautiful gift if we can just allow neutral awareness to occur, even momentarily. All the stories rush in, the list of slights, the reasons our rage /indignation/frustration/annoyance/disgust is so very justified. But if we realize through the gift of a message like Tolle's , that indignation and defendedness is not real power...it's illusory, empty, and can lead to tragedy if left unchecked by awareness.<br /><br />We observe in the present world we live in, the array of fear permutations doing their riotous blooming as paranoia, lack, defensiveness, self righteousness, retaliation, and the endless cycle of misery we know as reality and 'the news' in mainstream media. But those things grow in us too, in the dank closed up world the ego has created in us, trapping us (seemingly).<br /><br />It was the 'pain body' concept that has rocked my world and feels as if the heavens themselves opened and gave me a rope of light to climb out of my pain with. Gave me hope that I don't have to stay 'stuck' in a holding pattern of experiencing variations on a theme of the same old pattern of me 'not getting what I need' story.<br /><br />I think the term 'Pain Body' does not quite do justice to this phenomenon. When we are 'titillated' with schadenfreude, the delight of our 'enemies' or the 'elites' stumbling from their lofty perch, when we thrill to a roadside accident or our pupils dilate and hearts race with excitement in witnessing gratuitous violence, or even the smug horror I feel watching my reality show guilty pleasures....that also is feeding the 'pain body'. It indeed likes to 'feed' and its fare is anything arising out of human suffering. The ego is its handmaiden.<br /><br />The concept can resonate with many mythological archetypes including those in Christianity (I'm not technically a Christian but I was raised so), but for me I have never heard / read it described in terms that are so accessible, and in a manner that is gentle and not as harsh and cold as even some Buddhist concepts of samsara can be.<br /><br />(Tolle describes the Christ figure himself in his suffering as the embodied symbolic 'pain body' which seeks to be transmuted into pure awareness through 'allowing' and non resistance to 'what is'. (Forgiveness in Christian terms). The allowing and nonresistance can then give way to the real power of Presence (Paradise in Christian terms). Fighting and resistance continue the pain, allowing transforms it. This is the paradox of the crucifixion that always puzzled me as a child (why is it good that people suffer? why must we always look at this gruesome imagery or talk and pray about it? why was Judas bad if what Christ did was necessary and preordained? etc.)<br /><br />Amazing that the same message delivered at an earlier time in my life could not take root, but now, when I was open, it has indeed been received.y (I'm not technically a Christian but I was raised so), but for me I have never heard / read it described in terms that are so accessible, and in a manner that is gentle and not as harsh and cold as even some Buddhist concepts of samsara can be.<br /><br />(Tolle describes the Christ figure himself in his suffering as the embodied symbolic 'pain body' which seeks to be transmuted into pure awareness through 'allowing' and non resistance to 'what is'. B008A1TIOK|5.0|This sounds like complete blasphemy. Vivaldi's Four Seasons suite is a monument of classical music. It is a pillar of human art, so to have a young pup come along and pull it apart is enough for any fan, however casual, to start fuming in anger. What will stay the mob's pitchforks is the knowledge that said \\"pup\\" is Max Richter, nothing if not a sensitive, soulful artist, whose track record consists almost exclusively of touching people's souls with little more than a violin. This is not Philip Glass deconstructing David Bowie.<br /><br />Over 13 tracks (the 12 months and a short overture), Max Richter samples Vivaldi, sometimes faintly, sometimes closely, either distilling or expanding familiar pieces into something new, yet familiar, that adds a new layer to a masterpiece without detracting from the original. And what Max Richter brings to the table proves a game-changer, at least to this listener: he gives this music an aching heart. Vivaldi's originals are unique, brilliant, technical masterpieces, but sometimes, even in their best interpretations, they leave you cold, too admiring of their structural brilliance to be moved in a primal way. Richter collapses the distance and makes the 4 Seasons intimate, heartfelt.<br /><br />If you have even the remotest interest in classical, orchestral or even minimalist music, you owe it to yourself to hear this. At the very least it will be an interesting experiment, but if you open up to it, it will haunt you long after the last note fades to silence.

B008O9V4C2|4.0|Condos is more groove oriented than Morph, which is a good thing. These songs glide along in a funkier zone than some of Fagens recent studio efforts. The usual topics are covered with an increasing awareness of aging, giving songs like \\"Slinky Thing\\",and \\"The New Breed\\" a peculiar pathos and irony that only being 65 can. In \\"Slinky Thing\\", the writer observes how \\"we went to a party, everybody stood around think in' , hey what's she doing with a burned out hippie clown?.\\" Self deprecating humor like this is sprinkled throughout the album.<br /><br />\\"I'm Not the Same Without You\\" revisits the theme of separation explored on SDs \\"The Things I Miss the Most\\", although this time the protagonist isn't feeling sorry for himself so much as marveling over the newly improved person who is emerging out of the ashes. Unless of course, he's just trying to convince himself. A steady groover with a straightforward conversational tone, it's growing on me.<br /><br />One of Fagen's great strengths is to write songs as character study. \\"Memorabilia\\"  tells the story of an older guy who's obsessed with objects from the Cold War era, a nuclear doom collector if you will. Strangely catchy. The other character study and an indisputably \\"Dan worthy\\" tune introduces us to \\"Miss Marlene,\\" a fanatic bowler. It's the little details that make Fagens writing so memorable:\\"your move to the lane child, played on my heart strings, with your long skinny legs and your hoop earrings...\\" The album closer, \\"Planet d'Rhonda\\" is also a character study about yet another wild girl in Fagen's ever growing pantheon of irresistible trouble girls. A fun if perhaps not the most harmonically exciting tune on the album.<br /><br />In his mature years it's apparent Fagen has eschewed his penchant for penning obtuse lyrics for a straight ahead story telling approach and as such he is a master. Perhaps the standout example and my personal favorite so far is \\"The New Breed.\\" An age old story about an older guy having to deal with his young girlfriend going off with a younger dude, it stings and smolders with irony, sarcasm and self pity. \\"I get it- you look at me and think, he's ready for Jurassic park. He's sweet- but it's time to find a keener spark\\". Ouch.<br /><br />Rounding out the album are \\"Weather in My Head\\" a straight head but clever minor blues whose title spells out the gist of it, Good Stuff, a noirish gangland story executed in a typically streetwise Dan fashion, and a cover of Isaac Hayes \\"Out of the Ghetto\\", given a new meaning with a subtle Eastern European neo-Klezmer twist (check out those Balkan inflected horn parts - which ghetto are we talking about?) Thus far, these tracks have made the least impression on me, but I'm hanging in there, as past experience tells me Fagen's material often opens up after repeated listens.<br /><br />The production values are of course, flawless. The arrangements are funky and  tight- every part sits perfectly in the pocket, leaving lots of comfortable space around every instrument. Michael Leonhart did a fine job producing and holding down the drums, not to mention playing trumpet and arranging the horn parts along with Donald.<br /><br />Summing up, if you are a Dan or Fagen fan, you simply have to get this album. No, it's not his strongest work and no, it can't compare to the Nightfly for consistency and harmonic surprises, but next to most of the dreck that's out there, Sunken Condos shines with more than a handful of moments of pure brilliance.ing to deal with his young girlfriend going off with a younger dude, it stings and smolders with irony, sarcasm and self pity. \\"I get it- you look at me and think, he's ready for Jurassic park. Resuscitated from a self-perceived obsolescence, Pet Shop Boys presents monologues from the end of a love affair as a metaphor for the end of the public's love affair with the music of Pet Shop Boys? It's a dramatic idea, and I promise, the most fearless territory an artist can venture into. Questioning one's relevance and 'boy' status after being in the limelight for over 30 years is the polar opposite of going in front of a stadium and belting out \\"hope I die before I get old\\" in your mid 60s.<br /><br />Now for those who complain that Elysium isn't dancey enough, I like to remind you that's why recordings were invented. You have 30 years of PSB catalog to browse through.<br /><br />I would describe Elysium as a performance slow, steady, and sturdy by the musical maturity of self-assuredness. It also fights an internal battle against sarcasm and bitterness of age. How does one once soar at the top of the movers and the shakers, now \\"Invisible?\\" One of the greatest fear- once reserved for those in \\"the community\\" - is now a widespread fear of aging. \\"Should I hang it up and call it quits?\\" this body of work seems to be asking. This sort of honesty you'd expect from ungroomed folk singers, but not disco queens like the Pet Shop Boys. And it is this sort of self-interrogation that puts the boys many cuts above your average divas that go faster than they come.<br /><br />\\"Winner\\" sounds like some anthem one would expect to hear on Pride Weekend. Say what you will, but let us remember, even though he didn't come out in the 80s, Neil Tennant was pretty much in the open before musicians jumped on the bandwagon. He shows that he can be out about his age too: \\"Your Early Stuff\\" is pure humor, and shows the great delight of PSB where they can still laugh at themselves and their autumnal years (\\"What's in it for you? Need the Money?\\") Lush orchestration accompanies the ruminative \\"Breathing Space\\" as Tennant sings \\"far far away, I'm going, I gotta get out.\\"<br /><br />\\"Ego Music\\" basically surrenders completely to sarcasm, repeating \\"it's all about me me me.\\" It's the age old battle, do we laugh on the outside, or do we lash out with an acerbic remark about the present self-absorbed generation (conveniently forgetting that we ourselves were just as indulgent in our day).<br /><br />But an album called Elysium wouldn't live up to its name if there weren't the prospect of a second chance in the afterlife. \\"Hold on! Hold on! There's got to be a future!\\" opens the redemption act in this album. \\"Hold On\\" sounds like a glee club vocal ensemble, but what it really does it is to set the stage for classic Pet Shop Boys ahead.<br /><br />\\"Give it a Go\\" is optimistic, full of sunshine, and soulful medium tempo. \\"Memory of the Future\\" is unapologetically dramatic with \\"It's taken me all my life....to find you.\\" Swirls of electronica serve up musical hooks from a Gorgio Moroder film from the 80s, possible only by songwriters who have lived in that era.<br /><br />\\"Requiem in denim and leopardskin\\" is the crowning glory, the lily that asks for the gild, the violet that seeks the perfume. Urbane, polished, luxurious like the back of posh limousine going along city boulevards. All the great Pet Shop Boys ingredients are here: beautifully orchestrated strings, accompanying chorus, understated tempo, and carefully structured chords just the way you would want the movie of your life to close when the credits start to roll.<br /><br />\\"This is our last chance for goodbye, let the music begin,\\" Tennant sings, but the great treat of Elysium is if you happen to have your album playlist on repeat.  Because after the closing track stops to linger, Track 1 \\"Leaving\\" starts up again.  And in a metaphorical afterlife moment, you realize the song that first opened up Elysium now sounds totally different to your ears. That's what a great work of art does: it transports you on a journey andleaves you a different person with a different perception by the time you're done.<br /><br />The Pet Shop Boys will forever stay the Pet Shop Boys. They just make records that grow old, stowed away in some attic.leaves you a different person with a different perception by the time you're done.<br /><br />The Pet Shop Boys will forever stay the Pet Shop Boys. They just make records that grow old, stowed away in some attic.

0062060562|3.0|Before I Go to Sleep challenges readers to think about the relationship between memory and life, and the difficult process of life review, and journal writing.  S. J. Watson's character, Christine Lucas, has a form of amnesia that allows her to retain new information for only twenty-four hours.  When she sleeps she loses her memory, and must begin each new day with a blank mind.  Christine is desperate to find out who she is.  She wants to review her life.  She wants to understand her past.  But since she has no memory she must rely on her husband Ben, and her therapist Dr. Nash for information about her past. Dr Nash advises Christine to keep a journal so she can collect information about her life.<br /><br />  Watson uses first person to tell Christine's account, and Christine's questions become the plot of the story.  Each day she rereads her journal.  It becomes a substitute for her memory. A disturbing sentence in the beginning of her journal, \\"Don't trust Ben,\\" makes Christine and the reader aware of hidden evil.  The story slowly unfolds as both Christine and the reader learn more about the details of her past.<br /><br />  Any novel is important if it investigates universal ideas; Before I Go to Sleep does that. It explores the relationship between life and memory.  It narrates a fictional character's effort to find truth through life review and journal writing.  Early in the book Dr. Nash tells Christine she is not alone.  He says everyone, consciously or unconsciously, maintains a running narrative on the story of their life.  Everyone pieces together memories and thoughts to create that story.  But memory is faulty, so we must constantly revise and question our own facts.  Before I Go to Sleep defies the reader to think about these issues.  We may not be amnesiacs, like Christine, but at a certain age or after a traumatic experience most of us reflect on our past.  This is not an easy process, because it makes us question our previous narratives of our own life.  We are not that unlike Christine.n life.  We are not that unlike Christine.

0345803485|5.0|I have read many, many romance novels. Now, when I say many, I mean that's all I have on my bookshelf; with a few classics thrown in. I am pretty aware how the plot goes in a romance novel. With this book... That goes right out the window in the best, most infuriating way possible!!<br /><br />Spoiler Alert!!<br /><br />There is defiantly a reason why this book is for mature audiences only! Although it's not for the reasons that your thinking. Those scenes are very detailed (hellooo Mr. Gray!) and wonderful to read, but that's not all the book is about. When you read this book, you have to think outside the box and read between the lines. Look into what is happening with the characters emotions, not body. I read a lot of reviews about this book and all the ones that talk about abuse are way, way off. People see Christian as this Dom that only wants to hurt Ana, but that is not the case. If you pay attention he's actually not the Dom, she is. She is the one that is making demands of him, not the other way around. Every time she speaks up that she's uncomfortable with something, he stops; she doesn't. Ana is the one calling the shot, not Christian.<br /><br />You have to be able to read between the lines and see what is actually going on in their relationship. This is why I think only adults can fully appreciate this book. The writing is a little hard to get used to; but in no way, shape, or form does that determine the success of this book. I understand now the attraction 50 Shades of Grey. This is a great book, for those that will look beyond the surface.<br /><br />P.S. For my fellow hopeless romantics who read this, hold on to your seats... it's a rough ride!!!

0316228532|3.0|I am an avid reader and my home is small, so I've learned to categorize my books as 'one-time reads' and 'must own for life'.  One time reads are borrowed or loaded on the Kindle.  Must own books are hard copies to be kept forever.<br /><br />Since the author was Rowling I pegged 'Casual Vacancy' as a must own. I was disappointed and brought the book to work, left it in the reading room for someone else to take.  No need to read it again.<br /><br />Rowling has founded an organization - Lumos - to help underpriviledged children.  This purpose of this book seems to be to raise awareness.  I admire her for remembering her homeless days writing on napkins in a coffee shop.  Her fortune and fame have changed her into a person who can help, and she does.<br /><br />I gave 3 stars because Rowling is such an outstanding writer, not for the plot.  Casual Vacancy has multiple intertwined story lines, a typical small English village tale with Rowling's excellent character development and her ability to create another world for the reader to become a part of.  The problem here was, I didn't want to become part of this world and there was no character to identify with, the realism was too gritty.<br /><br />Maybe Rowling did this on purpose, to keep the reader as an outsider looking in.  Is she saying, lucky you, you have a choice and can escape this mess when you close the book, so please help those who live it and can't escape? Or maybe, please don't be the prig, fatty, adultress, child beater, pathetic drug addict or evil teen in your community, thanks.  What she explores is how the 'haves' desperately fear the 'have nots.<br /><br />Nearly every child in this book experiences hopelessness and despair.  They have to become tough in order to survive. I wanted some form of happy ending, or at least a kernel of hope by the end, but it never came.<br /><br />The most annoying of the villagers do get their comeuppence.. Shirley, Howard and Fats in particular.  And in most cases acharacters' biggest weakness was the thing that got them in the end, which was mildly satisfactory.<br /><br />Here's hoping Rowling will write another adult book and find the happy medium between HP and Vacancy.
